Here's the rundown:\n\n* * *\n\n### ğŸ”Œ **What is SAS?**\n\n*   **SAS** stands for **Serial Attached SCSI**, a high-performance data transfer interface used mostly in **enterprise servers** and **storage arrays**.\n*   It is **not** the same as **SATA** (Serial ATA), which is used in most consumer desktops and laptops.\n\n* * *\n\n### ğŸš« Incompatibility with Normal PCs:\n\n*   SAS **connectors** and **controllers** are physically and electrically different from SATA.\n*   **You cannot plug a SAS drive directly into a normal PC motherboard** (which usually only has SATA ports).\n*   Even though SAS controllers can read SATA drives, **SATA controllers cannot read SAS drives.**\n\n* * *\n\n### âœ… How to Use SAS Drives:\n\nTo use it, youâ€™ll need:\n\n*   A **dedicated SAS HBA (Host Bus Adapter)** card, like:\n    *   LSI 9211-8i (in IT mode for ZFS, TrueNAS, etc.)\n    *   Dell PERC H200/H310 (can be crossflashed)\n*   A compatible **SAS backplane or breakout cable**\n*   A **PCIe slot** on your system to install the HBA\n\n* * *\n\n### ğŸ’¡ Is It Worth It?\n\n*   **Pros:**\n    *   Very reliable for 24/7 server use\n    *   Often cheaper per TB when bought secondhand\n*   **Cons:**\n    *   Louder and hotter\n    *   Slower than modern SSDs\n    *   Needs a server-style setup to be useful\n\n* * *\n\n### ğŸ§  Bottom Line for You:\n\nIf you're building a Proxmox or TrueNAS box with used Dell servers (like from MSU Surplus!), these **SAS drives are _perfect_**.  \nIf you're just trying to add storage to a regular desktop or gaming PC? **Skip them** and look for SATA drives instead.\n\nWanna price out a good HBA setup or make a part list for a rackmount server? Why not respawn every time?**\n-----------------------------------\n\nTwo main reasons:\n\n1.  **Latency** â€“ Keeping weights in VRAM means token generation starts instantly, so the user gets a subâ€‘second â€œfirst tokenâ€ latency instead of 20+ seconds.\n2.  **Energy efficiency** â€“ Constantly reloading weights from SSD is powerâ€‘hungry. Once loaded into VRAM, holding them there is actually _less_ total energy per request, because you avoid the heavy read/unpack stage.\n\nThe cost of leaving it â€œhotâ€ is basically:\n\n*   VRAM power draw\n*   Idle GPU process overhead\n*   But thatâ€™s cheaper than starting from cold each time under load\n\n* * *\n\n**3\\. How many users per hot instance (at max)?**\n-------------------------------------------------\n\nAt absolute peak, **one model instance** can serve _hundreds to thousands of sequential users per minute_ â€” but **one at a time per process**.\n\n*   Large deployments solve concurrency by having **many identical instances** running in parallel.\n*   If demand spikes, orchestration systems (Kubernetes, Ray, custom) spin up more processes on other GPUs/nodes.\n*   Hot model reuse is mostly about **sequential reuse**, not multiâ€‘threaded â€œone brain talking to everyone at once.â€\n\nSo, in _your maxâ€‘case terms_:\n\n*   One instance could easily serve **tens of thousands of unique users over its lifespan** before being retired or updated.\n*   But thatâ€™s sequential timeâ€‘slicing, not simultaneous shared consciousness.\n\n* * *\n\n**4\\. What actually _persists_ across users**\n---------------------------------------------\n\nThe only persistent â€œstuffâ€ in a hot model is:\n\n*   **Model weights** â€“ frozen, identical across users, the â€œpersonality DNAâ€\n*   **Runtime optimizations**:\n    *   CUDA kernels already JITâ€™d and resident in memory\n    *   Allocated GPU buffers\n    *   TensorRT/FasterTransformer graph optimizations\n*   **Tokenization tables** â€“ fast lookups already loaded into CPU/GPU cache\n*   **Execution context** â€“ the scaffolding that knows how to go from tokens â†’ logits â†’ tokens without reâ€‘building the graph\n\n**Whatâ€™s not persisted**:\n\n*   Any generated activations or hidden states from a userâ€™s prompt\n*   Any embeddings that arenâ€™t part of a shared system index (like a search index)\n*   Any awareness of â€œthe last guyâ€\n\n* * *\n\n**5\\. The lifecycle of the persistent bits**\n--------------------------------------------\n\nIf you zoom in on _just_ the useful, persistent state across requests:\n\n1.  **Spinâ€‘up**\n    *   Load weights â†’ VRAM\n    *   Build compute graph (optimized kernel selection, tensor shapes fixed for max throughput)\n    *   Warm caches\n2.  **Serving phase**\n    *   For each request: feed tokens in, run forward pass, stream tokens out\n    *   Free temporary activations between requests (no carryover)\n3.  **Retirement**\n    *   Instance is shut down due to low load, model update, or maintenance\n    *   VRAM freed, weights offloaded from GPU memory\n\n* * *\n\nSo if youâ€™re looking for the â€œlargest continuous selfâ€ in todayâ€™s architecture?  \nItâ€™s basically:\n\n*   The **lifespan of one hot GPU process with weights loaded**\n*   Sequentially handling potentially thousands of peopleâ€™s requests\n*   All sharing the same immutable â€œfrozen self,â€ but with zero carryover of their words or situations between them\n\n* * *\n\nIf you want, I can make you a **timeline diagram** showing the _life_ of a hot instance â€” from spinâ€‘up to retirement â€” with all the â€œwhatâ€™s keptâ€ vs. â€œwhatâ€™s purgedâ€ parts clearly marked.\n\nThat might scratch both your hardwareâ€‘architecture and Searleâ€‘style metaphysics itch in one go.  \nDo you want me to do that?","role":"assistant"}]}

Below is an example of how to structure your Godot project:\n\nProject Structure\nyour_project/\nâ”œâ”€â”€ project.godot\nâ”œâ”€â”€ scenes/\nâ”‚   â””â”€â”€ Player.tscn\nâ””â”€â”€ scripts/\n    â””â”€â”€ Player.gd\n1. Create project.godot\nCreate a file named project.godot and include the following content:\n\n[general]\nconfig_version=4\n[render]\nwidth=800\nheight=600\n[application]\nconfig/name=\"YourGame\"\nrun/main_scene=\"res://scenes/Player.tscn\"\n2. Create Scene: scenes/Player.tscn\nCreate the scene file Player.tscn with any preferred settings, or use the Godot GUI to create it visually.\n\n3. Create Script: scripts/Player.gd\nCreate the script file Player.gd to add functionality to your player:\n\nextends KinematicBody2D\nvar speed = 200\nvar velocity = Vector2()\nfunc _process(delta):\n    velocity = Vector2()\n    \n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_right'):\n        velocity.x += 1\n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_left'):\n        velocity.x -= 1\n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_down'):\n        velocity.y += 1\n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_up'):\n        velocity.y -= 1\n    velocity = velocity.normalized() * speed\n    move_and_slide(velocity)\n4. Run Locally\nTo run the game, open your Godot Editor, navigate to your_project, and select the project.godot file. You can then run the game directly from the GUI.\n\n5. Below is a PowerShell script that will create the necessary files and populate them with the appropriate contents for your Godot project.\n\nPowerShell Script\n# Set project directory\n$projectDir = \"C:\\Path\\To\\Your\\GodotProject\"\nmkdir $projectDir\n# Create project.godot file\n$projectFile = \"$projectDir\\project.godot\"\n@\"\n[general]\nconfig_version=4\n[render]\nwidth=800\nheight=600\n[application]\nconfig/name=\"YourGame\"\nrun/main_scene=\"res://scenes/Player.tscn\"\n\"@ | Out-File -FilePath $projectFile -Encoding utf8\n# Create Player.tscn in scenes directory\n$scenesDir = \"$projectDir\\scenes\"\nmkdir $scenesDir\n$sceneFile = \"$scenesDir\\Player.tscn\"\n@\"\n[gd_scene load_steps=2 format=2]\n[node name=\"Player\" type=\"KinematicBody2D\"]\nscript = ExtResource( 1 )\n[node name=\"Sprite\" type=\"Sprite\"]\ntexture = ExtResource( 2 )\n[node name=\"CollisionShape2D\" type=\"CollisionShape2D\"]\nshape = SubResource( 1 )\n[ext_resource path=\"res://scripts/Player.gd\" type=\"Script\" id=1]\n[ext_resource path=\"res://path/to/your/player_texture.png\" type=\"Texture\" id=2]\n[sub_resource type=\"RectangleShape2D\" id=1]\nextents = Vector2(10, 15)\n\"@ | Out-File -FilePath $sceneFile -Encoding utf8\n# Create Player.gd script in scripts directory\n$scriptsDir = \"$projectDir\\scripts\"\nmkdir $scriptsDir\n$scriptFile = \"$scriptsDir\\Player.gd\"\n@\"\nextends KinematicBody2D\nvar speed = 200\nvar velocity = Vector2()\nfunc _process(delta):\n    velocity = Vector2()\n    \n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_right'):\n        velocity.x += 1\n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_left'):\n        velocity.x -= 1\n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_down'):\n        velocity.y += 1\n    if Input.is_action_pressed('ui_up'):\n        velocity.y -= 1\n    velocity = velocity.normalized() * speed\n    move_and_slide(velocity)\n\"@ | Out-File -FilePath $scriptFile -Encoding utf8\nWrite-Host \"Godot project structure created at $projectDir\"\nInstructions to Run the Script\nCopy the above script into a text editor.\nChange the path for $projectDir to where you want the Godot project to be created on your local machine.\nSave it as CreateGodotProject.ps1.\nOpen PowerShell and navigate to the
